Chapter Forty-Nine
On Incising Tumors That Occur Due to Arteries or Veins, Called Aneurysm
When an artery is wounded and the skin above it heals, a tumor often results, and similarly, a vein can also develop swelling and tumor.
The signs by which one knows whether the tumor and swelling are due to an artery or vein: if the tumor is due to an artery, it will be elongated and concentrated deep in the body, and when you press the tumor with your finger, you feel as if it has a squeaking sound.
That which is due to a vein will be round and on the surface of the body. Incising these tumors is dangerous, especially those in the armpit, groin, neck, and many other parts of the body, and if they are very large, you should avoid treating them with the knife.
Also avoid those in the extremities or head. For those caused by dilation of the artery opening, make a lengthwise incision in the skin, then open the incision with hooks, then peel away the artery and free it from the membranes.
Until it is exposed, then insert a needle underneath it and pass it to the other side, and tie the artery with a doubled thread in two places as I taught you in removing the arteries in the temples, then pierce with a lancet the area between the two ligatures until all the blood within it comes out.
Then the swelling dissolves, then apply the treatment that generates pus until the ligatures fall off, then treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If the swelling is due to a vein incision, you should hold with your hand as much of the swelling with the skin as you can, then insert a needle below the area you held with your hand and pass it through with a doubled thread until it emerges from the other side.
Then tie the swelling well with it as I mentioned to you regarding tying the grape-like growth from both sides with the ends of the thread, and if you fear the threads might slip, insert another needle with another thread under the entire swelling where the first needle intersects.
And tighten your threads in four places then cut the swelling in its middle until when what is inside comes out, cut off the excess skin and leave what was tied, then place on it a compress that you have dipped in wine and oil.
Then use the treatment that involves wicks and ointments until it heals.
Chapter Fifty.
On the swelling that occurs from nerve twisting.
Just as swelling occurs in the artery and vein, likewise swelling occurs in the nerve when it suffers a blow or occurs from excessive fatigue or the like, and this happens most often in the areas of the wrists and heel.
And in every place where joints move, it is a firm swelling whose color resembles the rest of the body and is usually without pain, and when pressed firmly the patient feels a kind of numbness, and the swelling is not gathered in the depth of the body.
Rather, it is under the skin and it moves in all directions but does not go forward or backward, and those that are in the joints should not be approached with iron [surgical tools] as it might cause permanent disability, and those that are in the head or forehead.
Cut the skin with a lancet, and if the swelling is small, hold it with forceps and cut it from the root, and if it is large, hang it with a hook and skin it then remove it and join the wound with stitching and treat it until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-One.
On cutting warts that appear on the abdomen.
Often some people develop on their abdomen and the rest of their bodies warts called mushroom-like because they resemble mushrooms, with a thin base and thick head whose edges have turned over, and some are small and some become very large.
Indeed, I witnessed a man who had two warts on his abdomen that most resembled mushrooms with no difference, white with thin bases and turned-over, cracked edges, with moisture constantly flowing from them, so I cut them and found the weight of one to be about eighteen ounces and the other about six ounces.
The procedure for cutting them is to examine, and if the patient is of moist temperament and the wart is white, moist, and thin at the base, cut it with a broad lancet and have cautery irons ready in the fire as often much blood gushes forth when cutting them.
So hurry if the blood overwhelms you and cauterize it, and if you see the patient is cowardly and frightened of cutting with iron, take a well-made lead thread and tie it around the wart of this description and leave it for two days, then increase the tightening of the lead, and continue to tighten the lead.
Whenever it affects the wart until it cuts through and falls off by itself without effort, but if the wart has a thick base, there is some fear and risk in cutting it, especially what is on the abdomen, but it is possible to cut half of it or some of it.
Then cauterize it so it doesn't return, then treat it until the wound heals, and beware of attempting to cut a wart that is dusky in color, with little sensation and ugly in appearance, for it is a cancerous tumor and we will discuss cancer after this.
Chapter Fifty-Two.
On the treatment of protruding navel.
Protrusion of the navel occurs from many causes: either from a split in the peritoneum covering the belly, from which omentum or intestine emerges as happens in other hernias, or from blood flowing from a vein or artery as previously mentioned, or from trapped wind.
If it is due to splitting of the peritoneum and protrusion of the omentum, then the color of the swelling resembles the body's color and is soft without pain and appears irregular in position.
If it is due to intestinal protrusion, its position along with what we described is more irregular, and when you press it with your fingers it disappears then returns, and sometimes there is gurgling with it and it enlarges considerably upon entering the bath and with severe exertion, and if it is due to moisture it will be soft.
It does not disappear when you press it with your hand and does not increase or decrease, and if it is due to blood then along with these signs the swelling appears blackish, and if it is due to growing flesh then the swelling is firm and hard and remains at one size.
If it is due to wind its touch is soft, and the procedure in this case is to examine - if the navel protrusion is due to arterial or venous blood or wind, then you should refrain from treating it as there is danger and risk in that, as I informed you in the chapter where I mentioned swellings that occur due to arteries and veins.
If the navel protrusion is due to intestine or omentum, you should instruct the patient to hold their breath and stand upright extended, then mark with ink around the entire navel.
Then order them to lie before you on their back, then make an incision with a broad scalpel around the navel at the place you marked with ink, then pull the center of the swelling upward with a large hook, then bind the incision site with strong thread or silk cord with a firm binding.
The binding should be a slip knot, then open the center of the bound swelling above the binding and insert your index finger and search for the intestine - if you find it has been caught by the binding, loosen the slip knot and push the intestine into the belly, and if you find omentum, pull it with a hook.
Cut off its excess, and if you encounter an artery or vein, tie it off well and return to your work, and take two needles and thread them with strong threads and insert the needles crossed through the incision you made around the swelling, having passed them through, then bind the swelling in four places on the needles.
If you wish, remove the needles and leave the site until the bound flesh rots and falls off by itself or cut it when it becomes thin and rotten, then treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals, and if the navel protrusion is from flesh growing in it.
Or from moisture, you should hollow out the swelling as we said and extract the blood or moisture you find in it, then treat it with what will heal the site.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
On the Treatment of Cancer.
We have mentioned in the classification the types of cancer and how to treat it with medicines and the warning against treating it with iron lest it ulcerate, and we mentioned cancer occurring in the uterus and the warning against treating it.
The ancients mentioned that when cancer is in a location where it can be completely excised, like cancer that occurs in the breast or thigh and similar accessible organs for complete removal, especially if it is early and small, but when it is old and large you should not approach it.
For I have not been able to cure anyone of it nor have I seen before me others succeed in that, and the procedure for it when it is accessible as we said is to begin by purging the patient of black bile several times then bleed them if there is clear fullness in the vessels.
Then position the patient in a position suitable for the procedure then cast into the cancer hooks appropriate for it then hollow it out from all sides along with the skin thoroughly until none of its roots remain and let the blood flow and do not stop it quickly.
Rather squeeze the sites and extract all the thick blood with your hand or whatever instruments possible, and if you encounter severe bleeding during the procedure from cutting an artery or vein then cauterize the vessel until the bleeding stops then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Four.
On the Treatment of Dropsy.
We have explained in the classification the types of dropsy, how water accumulates, the signs of each type and its treatment with medicines. The type treated with iron [surgery] is only the ascitic type alone, and the tympanitic type and the fleshy type should never be approached with iron.
For that is fatal. If you have treated this ascitic type of dropsy with medicines and your treatment was not effective, then observe if the patient has become extremely weak or has another illness besides dropsy such as having:
A cough or diarrhea or something similar, then beware of treating him with iron for it is dangerous. If you see the patient has abundant strength and has no illness other than dropsy alone, and is neither a child nor an elderly person, then the procedure is to have the patient stand before you.
And a servant behind him pressing his abdomen with his hands and pushing the water down toward the pubic area, then take a thorny scalpel of this shape:
Sharp on both sides, long with a pointed tip like a lancet, except that it has some slight flatness so that during the operation it doesn't penetrate into the intestines and harm them. Then observe if the dropsy has developed from the area of the intestines.
Then you should distance the incision from the navel by three fingers' width downward in line with it above the pubic area. If the dropsy developed due to liver disease, then make your incision to the left of the navel by three fingers' width. If it developed due to splenic disease, then make the incision on the right side by three fingers' width.
And also the incision should not be on the side that the patient wants to lie on, lest the fluids flow to that weak spot. Then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, then insert the instrument into that incision and raise your hand.
With the scalpel between the skin and the peritoneum as if you're skinning it, and the amount you skin should be about the size of a fingernail or so. Then pierce the peritoneum until the scalpel reaches an empty space, which is where the water is, then remove it and insert into the hole the instrument which is of this shape:
It is like a thin reed tube made of silver or copper or steel, smooth and polished, having a small hole at its bottom and three holes on its sides - two on one side and one on the other side as you see.
And its tip is sharpened in the shape of a pen nib of this shape:
At its upper end is a ring, for when the instrument reaches the water, it will immediately flow down the instrument. Draw out a moderate amount of water at the time, because if you draw out more than necessary at once, the patient might die from the dissolution of his vital spirit.
Or he might experience a faint close to death, but draw it out according to his strength and what the patient's condition indicates to you from his pulse strength and his good color. Then remove the instrument and stop the water, for it will stop immediately.
Due to the skin that holds the hole which is on the peritoneum that I told you to incise in that manner. Then return the instrument another day if you see the patient can tolerate it.
And draw out again a small amount of water, do this for days while being vigilant and careful of error until only a little water remains. If you fear for the patient and have left much water, then treat him by burying in hot sand.
And [encourage] profuse sweating in the bath and sun, and have him endure thirst and treat him with drying medicines until he recovers. And cauterize over the stomach, liver, and spleen after drawing out the water as I described previously.
Chapter Fifty-Five.
On the Treatment of Children Who Are Born with Their Urinary Openings Not Perforated or the Opening Is Narrow or Not in Its Proper Place.
Some boys come out of their mother's belly with their penis not perforated, so you should hasten to perforate it from the hour of birth.
With a very thin scalpel of this shape:
Then you place a thin lead nail in the hole and tie it and keep it for three or four days, so whenever he needs to urinate, remove it and let him urinate, then return it. If you don't use the lead, it's possible that the urine flowing over the area won't let it close.
As for one whose hole is narrow, it should be treated with lead as we said for many days until it widens. And those among them whose hole is not in its proper place, such that some are born with the hole at the tip of the penis and cannot urinate forward.
Until he lifts the urethra up with his hand, and he cannot have children because the semen cannot reach the womb in a straight path, and this is a very ugly condition. The method of operation for this is that the patient lies on his back.
Then stretch his penis firmly with your left hand and pare the tip of the urethra with a blade or sharp lancet like sharpening a pen, or as if you're carving something so that its middle protrudes like a penis and the hole falls in the middle as it should.
Be careful during your operation of blood loss as this often occurs, so counter it with what stops the blood and treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Six.
On tumors that occur in the foreskin and penis, and blackening and corruption, and adhesion of the foreskin to the penis.
This tumor often occurs in the urethra and it is an ugly fleshy protrusion, and it can be malignant or non-malignant. For the non-malignant, you should hook it with a fine hook.
And cut it until you clean it all, then apply cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it afterward with palm ointment until it heals. But if the tumor is malignant and ugly in color, you should use cauterization after cutting and scraping it.
If the tumor is in the foreskin of an uncircumcised person, and some of the tumor is inside the foreskin and some outside, you should remove the tumor that's inside first, and when it heals, then treat it from the outside.
Because if you treat them both together, you cannot guarantee the foreskin won't perforate. And blackening and corruption can also occur in the testicles and foreskin, so you should hollow out all that has blackened and is about to corrupt or has corrupted.
Then after that, smear on it honey with ground and sifted pomegranate peels and bitter vetch, then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals. If bleeding occurs, use cauterization with a crescent-shaped cautery of this form:
For cauterization is beneficial for both conditions, I mean bleeding and when the wound has corrupted. If the penis is corroded and goes entirely at some point, you should insert a lead tube into the penis passage so the patient can urinate through it. As for adhesion of the foreskin to the penis.
This adhesion only occurs in those whose foreskin is intact and who were not required to be circumcised, and its adhesion can occur due to a wound or swelling, so you should flay it with a flat lancet until the connection is loosened and the penis is freed from all sides.
If it's difficult to separate them thoroughly, you should flay some of the penis and the foreskin, as the foreskin is thin and might quickly perforate due to its thinness. Then separate between the foreskin and penis with a thin linen cloth that has been moistened in cold water so they don't adhere again.
Then treat with astringent wine until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Seven.
On circumcising boys and treating what errors occur to them.
Circumcision is nothing other than a disruption of continuity like other wounds, except that since it is done by our will and is used especially in boys, we must prescribe the best operation for it.
And the easiest path leading to safety. I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision in any of their books because it was not used in their laws, and it is only what we have acquired.
Through experience, and that is because I found the majority of craftsmen and cuppers using circumcision with the razor and scissors, and using the disk and thread tie and cutting with the nail, and I have tried all these methods.
I found nothing better than circumcision with scissors and tying with thread, for circumcision with a razor often causes the skin to retract, as the foreskin has two layers, and sometimes the upper skin is cut while the lower layer remains.
This necessitates another cut and renewed pain, and circumcision with the disk is not safe from cutting the tip of the penis as it might enter its hole, and as for circumcision with the nail, the skin might slip and your work would be ruined, or the child's skin might naturally be short.
Many are born thus not needing circumcision, and I have seen this. As for circumcision with scissors and tying with thread, experience has revealed its superiority to me because the scissors cut proportionally since the upper blade is like the lower blade.
When you squeeze your hand with the balanced blades, it cuts in one measurement and at one time, and the thread's restraint becomes like a wall for the penile skin from all sides, with no error occurring at all. The first procedure is to make the boy imagine.
Especially if he understands a little, that you are only tying the thread to his penis and will leave it until another day, then cheer him up and please him in every way possible that he can accept with his mind, then have him stand upright before you.
He should not be sitting, and hide the scissors in your sleeve or under your foot so the boy's eye never falls upon it or any of the instruments, then insert your hand to his penis and blow into the skin and lift it up until the head of the penis emerges.
Then clean it of any accumulated dirt, then tie the marked place with a doubled thread, then tie a second knot slightly below it, then hold the location of the lower tie firmly with your thumb and index finger and cut between the two ties.
Then quickly lift the skin upward and expose the head of the penis, then let the blood flow a little as it is better and reduces swelling of the penis, then dry it with a damp cloth, then sprinkle on it ash from burned dried gourd which is the best I have tried, or fine flour which is also excellent.
Then place on top of the powder in a cloth the white of an egg cooked in rosewater beaten with fresh, good-quality rose oil and leave it on until the next day, then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
And this is the image of the scissors that are suitable for circumcision:
They should be blunt-tipped and cutting with no crookedness, with a well-fitted screw, and the length of the blades should be equal to the length of the handles. As for errors occurring in circumcision, sometimes the inner skin is turned entirely or partially during cutting, so you should extend it immediately with your nail before the area swells.
And cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail then pull it with a hook and cut it. If three days pass and what remains under the head of the penis remains swollen and inflamed, leave it until the hot swelling subsides and peel it gently.
And cut it as becomes possible for you, and be careful of the head of the penis, for if something of the penis head is cut, it will not harm, so treat it with wound-healing powders that we described in the chapter on powders.
And if more skin than necessary is cut and it retracts upward, this also does not cause much harm, so treat it as we mentioned until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Eight
On the Treatment of Urine Retained in the Bladder
Urine retained in the bladder occurs due to blockage from a stone, clotted blood, pus, growing flesh, or similar things. If you have treated this with what we mentioned of the types of treatment described in the classification.
And the urine does not release and you see that its retention is due to a stone that has moved into the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be made to kneel on his knees, then a man should ride on his back and pull his belly toward his back, and the patient should hold his breath as long as possible.
Then the neck of the bladder will be forced to push the stone backward and the urine will release. If it does not release with what we mentioned and the matter becomes severe for the patient, then you should use extraction with the instrument called a catheter, which is this image:
It is made of silver and is smooth, hollow like a bird's quill feather in the thinness of the probe, about one and a half spans long, with a fine funnel at its head. The method of drawing urine with it is to take a doubled thread and tie a piece of wool or cotton to its end with a good knot.
Insert the end of the thread into the bottom of the catheter and cut with scissors any excess wool so it enters the tube and blocks it like a stopper. Then lubricate the catheter with oil, butter, or egg white, and seat the patient on a chair.
Irrigate their bladder and urethra with moist oils or oil and lukewarm water, then insert the catheter into the urethra gently until it reaches the base of the urethra, then bend the urethra upward toward the navel, then push the catheter inside it.
When the urethra is fully bent, push the catheter inside until when it reaches near the rectum, angle the penis downward with the catheter inside it, then push it until it reaches the bladder and the patient feels it has reached an empty space.
This procedure is done in this order because the urinary passage has a curve. Then pull the thread with the wool firmly but gently, as the urine will follow the wool, then remove it and the urine will flow, and reinsert the catheter.
Keep doing this until the bladder is emptied and the patient feels relief.
Chapter Fifty-Nine
How to irrigate the bladder with a syringe.
The instruments suitable for this are made of silver or ivory, hollow with a long tube as thin as pus, and if you want to instill waters and medicines into it, this is done with an instrument called a syringe, and this is its form:
It is made of silver or ivory, hollow with a long tube as thin as a probe, all hollow except the tip which is solid with three holes, two on one side and one on another side as you see.
The hollow space containing the plunger should be just enough to seal it without excess, so that when you pull with it any fluids are drawn in, and when you push with it they are expelled to a distance, like the sprayer used to shoot naphtha in naval battles.
If you want to introduce fluids into the bladder, insert the tip of the syringe into the fluid and pull the plunger upward so the fluid is drawn into the cavity of the syringe, then insert its tip into the urethra as we described for the catheter, then push the fluid with the plunger.
That fluid will reach the bladder immediately until the patient feels it, and this is the form of another fine irrigator with which to irrigate the bladder:
It is made of silver or lead, its upper head resembles a small funnel with a groove below it for the tie. Then take a camel's bladder and put in it the fluid with which you want to irrigate the bladder, then tie it firmly between the two grooves with a doubled thread.
Warm that fluid slightly over fire then insert the tip of the irrigator into the urethra, then press your hand firmly on the bladder with the fluid until the patient feels that fluid has reached the bladder.
If you don't have a bladder available, take a piece of parchment and make a circle from it and puncture it all around its circumference, then insert a strong thread through those holes around the circle, then gather the circle as you would gather a dining mat after you put in it whatever fluids, oils and waters you want.
Then tie it to the instrument and do with it as you did with the bladder by squeezing with your hand until the fluid reaches the bladder.
Chapter Sixty.
On Extracting Stones.
We have mentioned in the classification the types of stones and their treatment with medicines, and I described the difference between stones formed in the kidneys and stones formed in the bladder, and the signs of all that, and I mentioned the stones which require manual operation and incision.
These are specifically the stones formed in the bladder and those that get stuck in the urethra, and I will describe that with clear explanation and brevity.
I say that bladder stones most commonly occur in boys, and among their signs is that the urine exits from the bladder similar to water in its thinness.
Sand appears in it, and he scratches his penis and fiddles with it, and often it hangs down then spreads, and the rectum protrudes in many of them, and healing is easier in boys until they reach fourteen years, and difficult in the elderly, while for young men it is intermediate between these.
Those whose stone is larger are easier to treat, and small ones are the opposite of that, and when we proceed to treatment, first the patient should be given an enema to remove all the waste in his intestines, as it can prevent finding the stone during examination.
Then take the patient by his legs and shake him downward to make the stone descend to the neck of the bladder, or have him jump from an elevated place several times, then seat him upright before you with his hands under his thighs to make the entire bladder incline downward, then examine him.
Feel him from the outside, and if you sense the stone in the space, proceed immediately with the incision over it, but if you cannot feel it at all under your touch, you should oil the index finger of your left hand if the patient is a boy, or the middle finger.
If he is a full-grown youth, insert it into his rectum and search for the stone until when it falls under your finger, move it little by little to the neck of the bladder, then press on it with your finger and push it outward toward the place where you want to make the incision.
Order an assistant to squeeze the bladder with his hand, and order another assistant to pull up the testicles with his right hand, and with his other hand to pull the skin below the testicles away from the site where the incision will be made, then take the sharp scalpel which is of this form:.
And make an incision between the rectum and testicles, not in the middle but toward the left buttock, and let the incision be over the stone itself while your finger is in the rectum and you are pushing it outward at an angle so that the incision is wide on the outside and narrow on the inside, just enough to allow the stone's exit.
No larger, for perhaps pressing the finger in the rectum against the stone during the incision will make it come out without difficulty, and know that some stones have angles and edges which make their exit difficult.
And some are smooth like acorns and rounded, making their exit easy, so for those that have angles and edges, increase the incision slightly, and if it doesn't come out this way, you should try to manipulate it either by gripping it with a firm forceps whose tip is like a file.
To grip the stone so it doesn't slip away, or insert beneath it a fine tool with a hooked tip, and if you cannot manage it, widen the incision slightly, and if blood overwhelms you, stop it with vitriol.
If there is more than one stone, first push the larger one to the mouth of the bladder then make the incision over it, then push the smaller one after that, and do likewise if there are more than two, and if it is very large, it would be ignorant to make a very large incision for it because one of two things will happen to the patient.
Either he will die or he will develop constant urinary dripping because the site will never heal completely, but try to push it until it comes out or attempt to break it with hooks until you can remove it in pieces.
When you finish your operation, fill the wound with frankincense, aloe, and antimony, bind it, and place above it cloths soaked in oil and wine or rose oil and cold water to calm the hot swelling, then have the patient lie on his back and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
When it dissolves, bathe the area with plenty of water and oil, then treat it with palm ointment and basilicon ointment until it heals. If excessive hot swelling occurs in the wound, or erosion and similar issues such as blood clotting in the bladder and urine retention occur, this can be recognized by blood appearing in the urine.
Insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains it will lead to corruption and infection of the bladder. Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt, and treat each type with its corresponding treatment until it heals.
Throughout all treatment times, you should bind the thighs together to keep the medicines placed on the area in place. If the stone is small and has entered the urethra and become stuck there, preventing urine from exiting, treat it as I will describe before resorting to incision.
Many times I have found this treatment sufficient without need for incision, as I have tested it: take a steel probe of this shape:
Triangular at the tip, sharp, inserted into a handle. Then take a thread and tie the penis below the stone so it doesn't return to the bladder, then gently insert the probe's metal tip into the urethra until it reaches the stone itself.
Rotate the probe with your hand against the stone gradually while attempting to pierce it until you penetrate it from the other side, then urine will flow immediately. Then squeeze your hand on what remains of the stone outside the penis, as it will crumble and exit with the urine, and the patient will heal.
If this treatment is not possible due to some impediment, tie one thread below the stone and another above it, then make an incision on the stone in the penis itself between the two ties, then remove it.
Then untie the binding and clean the clotted blood that has accumulated in the wound. The thread must be tied below the stone to prevent it from returning to the bladder, and the upper tie is so that when the thread is removed after the stone's extraction, the skin returns to its place covering the wound.
Therefore, when you tie the upper thread, you should lift the skin upward so it returns after you finish and covers the wound as we mentioned.
Chapter Sixty-One
On Removing Stones from Women
Stones rarely form in women, but if one of them develops a stone, its treatment is difficult and prevented for many reasons: first, the woman might be a virgin; second, you won't find a woman who would allow herself to be examined by a physician.
If she is chaste or from those who are forbidden to be touched, and third, you won't find a woman who is skilled in this craft, especially in manual operations, and fourth, the location for incision to reach the stone in women is far from the stone's location, requiring a deep incision.
This is dangerous, but if necessity demands it, you should employ a skilled female physician, though they are rare to find. If one cannot be found, seek a chaste and gentle male physician, or bring a skilled midwife in women's matters, or a woman with some knowledge of this craft.
Bring her and instruct her to do everything you command regarding examining for the stone first, and that is to look - if the woman is a virgin, she should insert her finger into her rectum and search for the stone. If she finds it and can press it under her finger.
Then instruct her to make the incision on it. If she is not a virgin but previously married, order the midwife to insert her finger into the patient's vagina and search for the stone after placing her left hand on the bladder and pressing it well.
If she finds it, she should guide it from the bladder opening downward as far as possible until it reaches the base of the thigh, then make an incision opposite the middle of the vagina at the base of the thigh from whichever side is accessible and where she feels the stone in that area.
Her finger should not move from pressing under the stone, and the incision should be small at first, then insert the probe into that small incision. If she feels the stone, increase the size of the incision enough to allow the stone's removal, and know that there are many types of stones.
There are small and large ones, smooth and rough ones, long and round ones, and branched ones, so know their types to guide you to what you want. If blood overwhelms you, sprinkle powdered vitriol on the spot and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops, then return to your work.
Until the stone comes out. Know to prepare for yourself from the instruments that I mentioned for extracting stones from men to assist you in your work. If bleeding overwhelms you and you know from the blood's pulse that it's from a severed artery, put the powder on the spot.
Bind it firmly with bandages and leave it, do not return to it and leave the stone, do not extract it for the patient might perish. Then treat the wound, and when the blood's intensity subsides after days and the area becomes infected, return to your work until you extract the stone.
Chapter Sixty-Two.
On Incision for Hydrocele.
A hydrocele is the collection of fluid in the white membrane that lies beneath the scrotal skin surrounding the testicle, called the scrotum, and it may occur in a special membrane created by nature on one side of the testicle.
Until it appears to be another testicle, and it occurs between the scrotal skin and the white membrane we mentioned, but this happens only rarely. This hydrocele develops from weakness occurring in the testicles, causing this fluid to flow to them, and it may occur from a blow to the testicles.
This fluid can be of many colors: it may be yellowish, or bloody red, or sediment-like black, or watery white, which is most common. The signs by which it is known:
When water collects in the white membrane we mentioned, the swelling will be rounded, slightly elongated like an egg shape, and the testicle is not visible because the fluid surrounds it from all sides.
If the fluid is in its own special membrane, the swelling will be round on one side of the testicle.
For this reason, one might imagine it to be another testicle. If the fluid is between the scrotal skin and the white membrane, it will be palpable. If you want to know the color of the fluid, probe the swelling with the square probe whose image I presented earlier, and whatever comes out following the probe will indicate what's inside.
When we proceed to treatment with iron [surgical intervention], you should order the patient to be bled if possible and if you see their body is full, then have them lie on their back on something slightly elevated and place many cloths beneath them, then you sit on their left.
Order an assistant to sit on their right to pull their penis to one side of the scrotal skin and toward the lower abdomen, then take a wide scalpel and make an incision in the middle of the scrotal skin lengthwise near the pubic area.
Make the incision straight, parallel to the line that divides the scrotal skin in half until you reach the containing white membrane. Peel it away carefully without cutting it, and your peeling should be more from the side that adheres to the testicle, and peel as thoroughly as you can.
Then make a wide puncture in the fluid-filled membrane and drain all the water. Then separate the edges of the incision with hooks and pull the membrane upward without touching the containing scrotal skin, and cut the membrane however you can cut it, either entirely or piece by piece.
Especially its thin side, for if you don't cut it thoroughly, you cannot be sure the water won't return. If the testicle protrudes outside its covering during your operation, when you finish cutting the membrane, return it, then join the edges of the scrotal skin with sutures.
Then treat it like other wounds until it heals. If you find the testicle has been corrupted by another disease, you should tie off the vessels in the spermatic cord to prevent bleeding, then cut the testicle from the cord and remove it, then treat it as we mentioned.
If the collected water is on both sides, know that these are two hydroceles, so incise the other side as you did with the first one exactly, and if you can do both operations at once, do so. Then wipe away the blood.
Insert into the incisions wool that has been soaked in oil or rose oil, and place externally another wool soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over the testicles and lower abdomen, and place folded cloths on top, which are the dressings.
And bind them from above with a bandage that has six ends in this form:
Then take two pieces of cloth, sew them and stuff them with fluffed wool in this example, and make the ends that are tied with wet cotton or wool and gather them by tightening in the trouser belt, and one of the ends takes over the anus to the back.
The second goes toward the pubic area and the two ends on the thighs from below and the remaining two ends on the groins, and gather all the tightening in the trouser belt, and this hernia can also be treated with cauterization instead of cutting with iron.
Take a fine knife-shaped cautery and cut with it the skin of the testicle while it is hot as we described until the white membrane containing the water is exposed, then take another cautery in this form:
Which resembles the Greek eye, then pierce that membrane with it while hot until all the moisture comes out, then extend the membrane with hooks and strip with the cautery the containing layer and cut it as much as you can until you remove all of it, and protect the testicle so the fire doesn't touch it.
Know that this procedure is safer and further from blood loss and better than the cutting procedure, and if during cutting or cauterization you encounter hot swelling or blood loss or something else, you should treat whatever you encounter with the appropriate treatment as previously mentioned.
If the patient is fearful and cannot endure this procedure due to its horrific nature, let him use the puncture as I am describing, and this is when you have confirmed through the signs we presented earlier.
That the hernia is watery, the patient should sit on a high chair then puncture the swelling at its bottom with a wide lancet and make the puncture along the length of the body, and let the opening be wide until all the water flows out, then place cotton on the site and bind it.
And leave it to drain the remaining water, then treat it until the wound heals, and if the water's exit becomes difficult at the time of your puncturing, it is because the white membrane blocks the wound's opening and prevents the water's exit.
At that point, you should insert into the wound a goose feather or the instrument used to extract water from those with dropsy whose form was previously shown, or increase the wound opening slightly.
Know that the water may return and collect after six months or so, and when it collects, puncture it in the same manner and the patient will manage his days.
Chapter Sixty-Three
On Incision of Fleshy Hernias and Their Treatment
Know that incision on this hernia is among the dangerous procedures leading to death in most cases, therefore we see leaving it and staying safe from it, and I will mention the procedure for it and types of swelling.
I say that many swellings occur in the bodies that make up the testicles, and this happens from many causes, either from sharp excess flowing to the testicles or from a blow, and the swelling's color matches the body color and no water is found in it.
The swelling is firm and sometimes the swelling is hardened with a dull color and has no sensation, and it may be from knotted arteries and their inflation as previously mentioned or from vein inflation, and what comes from arterial inflation is known by the swelling's dissipation.
When you press it with your fingers and it should not be interfered with at all, and as for what comes from vein inflation, nothing dissipates from it when pressed with fingers, and this type can be cut into along with other flesh.
And it is that you cut the skin of the testicle then pull the testicle upward and remove it from the white membrane and separate the hanging part from the vessels and tie the vessels and cut the hanging part after separating it from all sides of the testicle, and if the testicle has fused with those growing flesh.
You should remove the testicle and cut it, and if there is adhesion between any of the membranes or between the vessels, you should detach all of that adhesion and cut it in a circular manner.
If there is flesh growth in the place of adhesion which is from behind, you should cut all of it and remove the testicle as we said, and when your work is complete, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Four.
On the Treatment of Hydrocele with Varicocele.
Varicocele is a somewhat twisted swelling resembling a cluster [of grapes] with relaxation of the testicles, making movement, exercise, and walking difficult for the patient, and in treating this condition there is risk similar to what was mentioned before.
But we should mention the procedure for it as the ancients did, so I say that you should seat the patient on a high chair, then push the testicular suspension downward, then hold the skin of the testicle with your fingers along with the vessels that are close to the penis.
Another assistant should hold it and pull it strongly, then you make an oblique incision with a sharp, wide scalpel along the vessels until the vessels are exposed, then separate from all sides as I mentioned to you in the extraction of temporal arteries, then insert a needle with a doubled thread.
And tie it at the beginning of the areas where the varicocele occurred and tie it also at its end, then make a vertical incision in the middle along the length of the body and remove what has accumulated in it of turbid, corrupt fluids.
Then treat the wound with the treatment of other wounds where you want pus to form so that the vessels that nourish one of the testicles fall off, and there is no harm in that, and if the varicocele affects all vessels, you should remove one testicle with the vessels so that the testicle is not deprived of nutrition.
Before cutting the vessels so it doesn't wither and become useless.
Chapter Sixty-Five.
On the Treatment of Intestinal Hernia.
This hernia occurs from a split that happens in the peritoneum extending over the abdomen near the groins from the lower abdomen, so the intestine flows from that hernia to one of the testicles.
This hernia occurs either from splitting of the peritoneum or from its stretching, and these two types occur from many causes: either a blow, or a jump, or a shout, or lifting something heavy and the like, and its sign when it's from stretching of the peritoneum is that it occurs gradually over a long time.
It doesn't occur suddenly and the swelling is even towards the depth because the peritoneum squeezes the intestine, and its sign when it's from splitting of the peritoneum is that it causes great pain suddenly from the start and the swelling is irregular, appearing under the skin nearby.
That's due to the intestine coming out and moving outside the peritoneum, and sometimes the omentum comes out with the intestine so this hernia is called intestinal and omental, and it can occur with wind, and sometimes feces flows in the intestine and gets trapped there, leading to the patient's death.
Because it causes severe pain and gurgling, especially when squeezed, and treating types of this condition with iron [surgery] is dangerous so you should be cautious about undertaking it, and the procedure description is to order the patient to return the intestine with his hand into his inside if it's possible to return.
Then he should lie on his back before you and raise his legs, then you stretch the skin near the groin upward and make a lengthwise incision in all of the scrotal skin, then insert hooks in the edges of the incision according to what's needed to open the incision with them.
The incision should be large enough for the testicle to come out through it, then separate the membranes under the scrotal skin until when the white hard peritoneum is exposed from all sides, at that point insert your index finger next to the testicle.
Between the white peritoneum under the scrotal skin and the second peritoneum and release with it the adhesion behind the testicle, then fold with the right hand to the inside of the scrotal skin while also pulling the white peritoneum upward with the left hand and lift the testicle with the peritoneum toward the incision.
Order the assistant to pull the testicle upward, and you completely release the adhesion from behind, and examine with your finger lest there be any twisted intestine in the hard white membrane, and if you find any of it, push it down into the abdomen.
Then take a needle with thick thread twisted from ten threads and insert it at the end of the membrane beneath the scrotal skin near the incision, then cut the ends of the thread's fold until there are four threads.
Then overlay them on each other in a cross pattern and bind with them the membrane which we said is under the scrotal skin with tight binding from two sides, then also wind the thread ends and bind them tightly so that none of the vessels that nourish it can reach anything to it.
Lest a hot swelling occur from that, and also make a second binding outside the first binding, distant from it less than two fingers, and after these two bindings leave from the membrane under the scrotal skin the size of a finger.
And cut all the remainder in a circular manner and remove the testicle with it, then make an incision below the scrotal skin from which blood and pus can drain as we described previously, then use wool soaked in oil and place it in the wound and use the binding we described.
And the white membrane we mentioned may be cauterized after cutting it as a precaution against bleeding, as this often occurs, and leave the binding until it falls off by itself, and if its falling is delayed, then irrigate it with hot water and apply what makes it separate until it falls.
Then treat the wound with the rest of wound treatments until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Six.
Regarding wind hernia: This wind hernia, I have not seen anyone dare to treat it with iron [surgical instruments], though the ancients mentioned to do as we described in hernia with varicocele, which is to bind the vessels gently below after making an incision on them.
Then make an incision in the middle and treat the swelling with what opens it until the vessels fall off, and treat the wound as we mentioned until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Seven.
On inguinal hernia.
Hernia occurs in the groin as we said, and the area swells but nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles, and if it does descend, it is minor and returns at all times.
But if time passes, the split in the membrane increases until the intestine and omentum descend into the scrotum, and this occurs from the stretching of the membrane that is in the groin as we said.
That is, the membrane stretches then relaxes and the area swells and protrudes, and its treatment is by cauterization as I described previously.
And it may be treated with iron [surgical instruments] in this manner: have the patient lie on his back before you, then make a transverse incision at the site of the protruding swollen hernia about three fingers in size, then cut through the membranes under the skin.
Until when the white membrane next to it is exposed, take a probe and place it on the protruding area of the membrane and press it into the depth of the abdomen, then stitch the two protruding areas at the tip of the probe from the membrane and join them together with the stitching.
Then withdraw the probe tip and do not cut the membrane at all, and do not touch the testicle or anything else as I taught you in treating intestinal hernia, then treat it with wound treatments.
When the threads break, clean them and heal the wound until it closes, for the membrane will contract and the hernia protrusion will not increase.
And cauterization is better in this location because it is closer to safety.
Chapter Sixty-Eight.
On relaxation of the scrotal skin.
Often the scrotal skin relaxes in some people without the flesh inside it relaxing, and its appearance becomes ugly, so for whoever desires to treat it, the patient should be laid on his back.
And cut all the skin that has relaxed on the thick skin then bring together the lips [edges], and if you wish to first stitch the excess relaxed skin with three or four stitches and secure the stitching then cut between the stitches.
Then treat it with treatment of other wounds until it heals and the threads fall out.
Chapter Sixty-Nine.
On Castration.
Castration is forbidden in our religious law.
For this reason, I should not mention it in my book, but I mention it for two reasons: first, so that the physician has this knowledge when asked about it and knows how to treat someone affected by it, and second, because we often need to castrate certain animals for our benefit.
Like lambs, billy goats, cats, and similar animals. I say that castration is done in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting and incision. As for the crushing method, the procedure is that we place the animal in hot water until its testicles relax, soften, and hang down.
Then you crush them with your hand until they dissolve and cannot be distinguished by touch. As for castration by cutting and incision, you should hold the animal and squeeze the skin of its testicles with the left hand, then tie off the attachments and make one incision on each testicle.
When the testicles emerge, cut them after skinning them, and don't leave any membranes on them except the thin membrane that covers the vessels. This type of castration is better than the crushing method.
Because crushing might leave some of the testicles remaining, causing the animal to still desire mating. Then treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Seventy.
On Treating Intersex Conditions.
Intersex conditions in men occur in two types: one where there appears in the perineal area or in the scrotal skin between the testicles a structure that looks like a woman's vulva with hair, and sometimes urine flows from the one that occurs in the scrotal skin.
As for women, there is one type, occurring above the vulva on the pubic area like small male genitalia protruding outward, one like a male penis and two like testicles. The treatment for all three types:
For the two types in men and the one type in women, one should cut away the excess flesh until its trace is eliminated, then treat it like other wounds until it heals. As for the second type in men where urine comes out through the scrotal skin, there is no treatment for it and no cure at all.
Chapter Seventy-One.
On Removing the Clitoris and Protruding Flesh from Women's Genitals.
Sometimes the clitoris increases in size beyond what is natural until it becomes unsightly and ugly, and in some women it becomes so large that it becomes erect like men's and leads to sexual intercourse.
One should hold the excess clitoris with your hand or a hook and cut it, but don't cut too deeply, especially at the base, lest bleeding occur.
Then treat it like other wounds until it heals. As for the protruding flesh, it is flesh that grows in the mouth of the uterus until it fills it.
Sometimes it protrudes outward like a tail.
Therefore, some ancients call it the tail disease, and it should be cut just like the clitoris and treated until it heals.
Chapter Seventy-Two.
On Treating Imperforate Vagina.
Imperforate vagina is when a woman's vagina is not perforated or when the opening is too small, and it can be either congenital, present at birth, or acquired. The acquired type occurs from a previous condition and can be either from excess growing flesh.
Or from a thin or thick membrane, and it can be either deep in the uterus, or on its sides, or at its top or bottom, and it prevents intercourse, pregnancy, and childbirth, and sometimes menstruation. This condition is diagnosed by the midwife's examination.
If the obstruction is visible and close, but if it isn't visible, she examines it with her fingers or a probe. If the obstruction is from a thin membrane and is close to the labia, proceed to pierce it by placing something like pads on the labia, then place both your thumbs.
With the woman on her back, legs spread, then stretch the labia forcefully until the thin membrane tears and the obstruction opens. Then take wool, soak it in oil, and place it on the area, and have the woman engage in intercourse daily so that the area doesn't heal shut again.
If the peritoneum is thick and dense, it should be incised with a wide scalpel resembling a myrtle leaf, and if the blockage is from growing flesh, grasp it with hooks and cut it, keeping with you medications that stop bleeding without stinging, such as acacia, gallnuts, and frankincense mixed with egg white.
Then use a wide lead tube so that the wound does not heal too quickly, keep it for days and use a dry cotton wick, then treat with the rest of the healing treatment until it heals, and if other flesh growths occur in the uterus, they should be cut in this manner.
Unless it is a cancerous tumor, for the cancerous tumor that occurs in the uterus should not be approached with iron [surgical tools] at all.
Chapter Seventy-Three.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, warts, and red pustules that occur in women's genitals.
As for hemorrhoids, it is the swelling of blood vessel openings until much blood continuously flows from them, and when hemorrhoids advance they become warts, and I have mentioned in the classification their types and signs, and we mention here.
What of them accepts treatment and what does not accept treatment, and I say that when hemorrhoids and warts are deep in the uterus and not sensible to touch, there is no treatment with iron [surgical tools], and those that are at the mouth of the uterus that can be sensed are those that are treated.
The woman should enter a cold room, then stretch the warts with forceps or rough cloth and cut them from their roots, then sprinkle upon them when bleeding occurs one of the non-stinging blood-stopping powders.
Such as acacia, gallnuts, frankincense and the like, then raise her legs against the wall for an hour, then lower them into cold water, and if bleeding continues, sit her in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate peels, oak galls and the like, then take barley flour and knead it with honey and vinegar.
And compress it on her back, and if the bleeding stops, fine, otherwise apply cupping glasses to the spine and breasts without scarification, then take wool and soak it in broomrape juice or plantain juice or blackberry branch juice with astringent wine and apply to the area.
When the swelling subsides, treat the area with ointment until it heals, and as for the red pustules, they resemble the heads of thyme, rough in appearance, and what appears of them should be cut according to what was mentioned for warts exactly and treated until healed.
Chapter Seventy-Four.
On lancing the abscess that occurs in the uterus.
Many types of tumors occur in the uterus such as cancer, hardened tumor, ulcers, abscess, gangrene, fistulas, hemorrhoids, fissures, warts, and hot swelling, and I have mentioned all these diseases and their types and signs in the classification.
We should mention in this article the hot swelling that occurs in the uterus when it is among the tumors that collect pus, how it should be lanced with iron [surgical tools], and you should observe if the pain of the tumor in its beginning is acute with throbbing, inflammation and fever.
And if you see it is red when touched, do not hasten to lance it and treat it with what helps maturation until when these symptoms subside, then the woman should sit on a chair with two seats and lean on her back.
And gather her legs toward the lower abdomen with her thighs spread apart and place her arms under her knees and tie them with a suitable binding.
Then the midwife sits on the right side and uses the instrument that opens the mouth of the uterus, whose illustration will come later, and when you want to use this instrument, you should measure with a probe the depth of the woman's uterus lest what enters of the instrument be more than the depth of the uterus.
For it would harm the patient, and if the instrument is longer than the depth, pads should be placed on the lip of the cervix to prevent the entire instrument from entering the depth of the uterus, and the screw that runs in the instrument should be placed on the upper side.
You hold the instrument while the assistant turns the screw until the cervix opens. When the abscess appears and can be felt by hand, and if it is soft and thin, it should be incised at its head with a wide lancet once all the pus has been drained.
A soft wick soaked in rose oil or green oil with some astringent should be placed in the wound, with the wick protruding from the incision in the cervix, and clean wool soaked in water boiled with mallow should be placed externally on the uterus and pubic area.
After two days, treat with the appropriate ointment until healed.
The uterus and wound should be washed by injecting water and honey, then with water boiled with licorice root or long birthwort, then return to the ointment. If the abscess is hidden deep in the uterus,
One should refrain from treating it with metal instruments and instead treat it as we mentioned in the classification.
Chapter Seventy-Five:
On teaching midwives how to treat living fetuses when they emerge in non-natural positions.
The midwife should first know the natural form of birth. Among its signs: when you see the woman pushing downward, desiring to breathe air, and her labor becoming easier,
And the fetus emerging quickly, know that this birth is in the natural position, with it emerging head-first and the placenta with it or attached to its umbilical cord. When you see these signs, you should press her abdomen so the fetus emerges quickly.
For when it descends head-first, the placenta descends with it and cleanses well of those fluids. Any birth other than this is unnatural and unfavorable, as the fetus may emerge feet-first, or with hands before head and feet,
Or with one hand or one foot, or emerge with head and hand together, or emerge folded, or sometimes turned onto its back, and other such unfavorable positions. The midwife should be skilled and gentle with all these things and be wary of errors and mistakes.
I will explain each position and how to deal with it so you can recognize and understand it. If the fetus emerges head-first in the natural way but this becomes difficult for the woman, and labor becomes hard for her, and you see her strength has weakened, seat her on a chair and instruct women to hold her.
Warm her uterus with cooked fenugreek and moist oils. Then the midwife should insert a small lancet between her fingers and cut the placenta with it, or cut it with her fingernail until its fluid flows out, and press the woman's abdomen until the fetus descends.
If it doesn't descend, the woman should be given an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil, then after the enema instruct her to push and make her sneeze with hellebore while holding her mouth and nose closed, and the fetus will emerge immediately. If the fetus's hands emerge first, they should be gently pushed back little by little.
If they cannot be inserted, place the woman on a platform and raise her legs upward, then shake the platform on the ground while the woman is held so she doesn't fall during the shaking. If the hands won't go in and the fetus has died, cut them off and pull out the rest of the fetus.
Or tie its hands with a cloth and pull them steadily and it will emerge. Regarding feet-first emergence: when the fetus emerges feet-first, these should be pushed upward, then gradually turn the fetus until it's properly positioned, then take one of its feet and pull it gradually.
When both have emerged to the thighs, instruct her to push and make her sneeze with hellebore and it will emerge. If it doesn't emerge as we described, then return the fetus gradually until it's in the natural position and it will then emerge smoothly. If it refuses despite all we described,
Take marshmallow mucilage, fenugreek mucilage, sesame oil, and dissolved gum, beat all together well in a mortar, then apply it to the woman's vagina and lower abdomen, then seat her in lukewarm water up to the hypochondrium.
When you see that its lower part has softened, make a suppository from myrrh and have her use it. When she has held the suppository for an hour, seat her on the chair, then make her sneeze and cover her mouth and nose, and gently press the lower part of her belly, for the fetus will emerge immediately, the fetus emerging on its knees and hands.
If it emerges in this manner, work to insert its hands little by little, then have the woman lie on her back and lower her legs while lying on a bed, and fold her arms, then press above her belly little by little.
Then remove the pillows from under her legs until she is positioned lower, and if the fetus does not emerge, take both her legs and move them vigorously, then press above the hypochondrium little by little until the fetus moves upward, then the midwife should insert her hand and adjust the fetus little by little.
And tell the woman to push until the fetus emerges, the fetus emerging sideways with one hand hanging down, work to return its hand, and if you cannot return it, make the woman stand and have her walk, and if she cannot walk, have her lie on.
Her bed and shake her legs vigorously, then apply the emollient I described made from mucilages, and if labor pains come to her, seat her on the chair, then work to return the hand and position the fetus in its natural position, and make the woman sneeze and tell her to push until it emerges.
The fetus emerging on its back with arms extended and its face toward its mother's back, the midwife should hold the fetus's hand then turn it little by little and adjust it gently, and when it is properly positioned, apply to her vulva what we described of oil and mucilages.
Then tell her to move little by little, and when she has done that, seat her on the chair and tell her to lean to the right side, then tell her to push and make her sneeze with hellebore and it will emerge, the fetus emerging upright on its side.
If it descends to the mouth of the uterus in this manner with the placenta, tear the placenta with your nail until it empties of fluid, and if it clings to the fetus's face and neck, cut it from the navel lest it suffocate and die, then push the fetus inward until you position it as needed.
And tell the woman to push several times and it will emerge easily, the emergence of twins or multiple fetuses, know that twins are often born and sometimes three or four are born and live, though this is rare, and as for five, it is something unnatural and they do not survive at all.
They are surrounded, even if numerous, by a single placenta and are separated by a membrane barrier between them attached to each one's navel, and they may emerge as a single fetus emerges in a natural, easy emergence, and they may emerge in a problematic emergence as we described.
If some of them are difficult during birth and take on the unnatural positions we mentioned, treat it as we described, and let the midwife be gentle and do what she does with gentleness and patience and devise for each position what strategy is available to her that leads to safety.
Mention of what forms in the uterus of fetuses that miscarry, there may form in the uterus one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and more than ten, and it has been confirmed to me that one woman miscarried seven and another fifteen, all of them formed, that.
By the decree of the Mighty, the Knowing, so all this should be in the midwife's knowledge for perhaps something like this will come to her one day and she will handle it as needed.
Chapter Seventy-Six.
On Extracting the Dead Fetus.
If you have treated the dead fetus with what I mentioned in the classification of treatment and it does not emerge, and you are forced to work by hand, you should observe, and if the woman is of sound strength and does not have any of the symptoms that make one fear her destruction, the woman should lie on a bed on her back.
With her head tilted downward and her legs raised, and a servant should hold her from both sides or she should be tied to the bed lest her body be pulled when drawing the fetus.
Then moisten her womb's opening with moist oils along with marshmallow mucilage, fenugreek, and flaxseed, then the midwife should oil her hand with these oils and mucilages, then insert it gently into the womb, then search for a place to insert the hooks into the fetus, and the appropriate locations for that.
Look, if the fetus is positioned to descend head-first, insert the hooks into its eyes, or nape, or mouth, or palate, or under its chin, or collarbone, or in places near the ribs or under the cartilages.
And if it is descending feet-first, then into the pubic area and middle ribs, and the hook should be held with the right hand with its curve between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the hand gently and plant a hook in some of those places we mentioned.
Until reaching an empty space, then plant opposite it another hook or a third if needed so the pulling is equal and doesn't lean to one side, then pull evenly and the pulling should not only be straight but moved in every direction.
To ease its exit as is done with a tooth when extracting it, and between that the pulling should be relaxed, and if a part becomes stuck, the midwife should oil some fingers with oil and insert them from that direction to turn what is stuck, and if part of the fetus emerges, move the hooks to other locations.
Slightly higher, do this until the entire fetus emerges, and if a hand emerges before others and cannot be returned due to compression, it should be wrapped with a cloth then pulled until when it fully emerges, cut it.
Either at the wrist joint or at the elbow, and thus should be done with the other hand and the feet, and if the fetus's head is large and experiences compression during exit or has accumulated fluid in its head, you should insert between the fingers a thorn-like lancet.
And split the head with it so the water comes out, or crush it with the tool called the crusher which will be illustrated along with other tools in the next chapter.
Likewise do this if the fetus naturally has a large head, you should split the skull or crush it with the crusher as we said, then remove the bones with hooks, and if the head emerges and becomes compressed at the collarbone, split it so the moisture in the chest flows out.
For the chest will collapse then, and if the chest doesn't collapse and cannot emerge, cut it into pieces as you can, and if the lower abdomen is swollen or has dropsy, you should pierce it until the fluid flows from it.
If the fetus is feet-first, then pulling it is easy and aligning it to the mouth of the womb is simple, and if it becomes compressed at the abdomen or chest, you should pull it with a cloth wrapped around your hand and split the abdomen or chest until what's in them flows out.
If all the limbs are extracted and the head retracts and becomes stuck, the midwife should insert the left hand, and if the mouth of the womb is open, insert the hand into the neck of the womb and search for the head and pull it with the fingers to the mouth of the womb, then insert into it one or two hooks and pull it with them.
If the mouth of the womb has closed due to hot inflammation that occurred in it, you should not be forceful with it, but rather then use the pouring of moist, greasy substances and use poultices and have her sit in waters that relax and moisten.
And if the fetus is on its side, if it can be straightened then use what we mentioned for the living fetus, and if that's not possible then cut it into pieces and remove it, and nothing from the placenta should be left inside at all, and when you finish your treatment, use what we mentioned of treatment for hot inflammations that occur in wombs.
And if bleeding occurs, have her descend into astringent waters and use the rest of the treatment, and I have witnessed a woman who was pregnant and the fetus died inside her, then she became pregnant again on top of it another time.
Then the other fetus also died, and after a long time she developed a swelling in her perineum that became inflamed until it opened and began discharging pus. I was called to treat her, and I treated her for a long time, but the wound would not heal, so I applied some strong drawing ointments to it.
A bone emerged from the site, then after some days another bone emerged, which surprised me since the abdomen is a place without bones. I surmised they were from the bones of the dead fetus, so I examined the wound and extracted many bones from it, bones from the fetus's skull.
I continued pursuing this until I had extracted many bones, while the woman was in the best of conditions. She lived like this for some time with a small amount of pus discharging from the site. I have included this rare case here.
Because it contains knowledge and assistance for what the physician-practitioner needs to do with his hands in treatment.
Chapter Seventy-Seven
Containing illustrations of instruments needed for extracting the fetus.
Illustration of a screw device for opening the mouth of the uterus:
This is like the clamp used to bind books evenly - it has two screws at the ends of two wooden pieces, except that this screw should be more delicate than the clamp and should be made either of ebony or boxwood, with each wooden piece being two fingers thick.
Their edges about a finger's width, their length a span and a half, and in the middle of the wooden pieces are two probes of the same wood type firmly fixed in them, their length half a span or slightly more, and their width about two fingers or slightly more, and these two probes.
These are what enter the mouth of the uterus to open it when you turn the screws. Illustration of another instrument for the same purpose, more delicate and lighter:
It is made of ebony or boxwood in the shape of forceps, except that it has two probes at its end as you see, each probe about a span long and two fingers wide. When you want to open the uterus with it.
Have the woman sit on a bed with her legs hanging down and spread apart, then insert these two probes closed together into the mouth of the uterus while you hold the end of the instrument below between her thighs, then open your hand with the instrument as you would with forceps, according to how much you want to open the uterus.
Until the midwife can do what she needs to do. Illustration of another screw device mentioned by the ancients:
